\end{TODO}

\hypertarget{r6}{%
\chapter{R6}\label{r6}}

\hypertarget{classes-and-methods}{%
\section*{14.2 Classes and methods}\label{classes-and-methods}}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{14.2 Classes and methods}

\begin{question}

\begin{quote}
Any \ldots{} R6 method called for its side effects \ldots{} should return invisible(self).
\end{quote}

WHY? What is \texttt{invisible(self)} doing in the add function below? I tried removing this line but it doesn't change the output\ldots{}

\end{question}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{Accumulator <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{R6Class}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Accumulator"}\NormalTok{, }\KeywordTok{list}\NormalTok{(}
  \DataTypeTok{sum =} \DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{,}
  \DataTypeTok{add =} \ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{x =} \DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{) \{}
\NormalTok{    self}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{sum <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{self}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{sum }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{x }
    \KeywordTok{invisible}\NormalTok{(self)}
\NormalTok{  \})}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{x <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{Accumulator}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{new}\NormalTok{()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Returning \texttt{self} or \texttt{invisible(self)} allows for method chaining. i.e. \texttt{x\$add(1)\$add(2)} can be done rather than \texttt{x\$add(1);\ x\$add(2)}. In the absence of anything better to return, why not return itself

\hypertarget{important-methods}{%
\section*{14.2.2 Important methods}\label{important-methods}}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{14.2.2 Important methods}

\begin{question}

Why don't we need to specifically call \texttt{haldey2\$print} to see the output below)? Is the print method just a built in output of an \texttt{R6} object?

\end{question}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{Person <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{R6Class}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Person"}\NormalTok{, }\KeywordTok{list}\NormalTok{(}
  \DataTypeTok{name =} \OtherTok{NULL}\NormalTok{,}
  \DataTypeTok{age =} \OtherTok{NA}\NormalTok{,}
  \DataTypeTok{initialize =} \ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(name, }\DataTypeTok{age =} \OtherTok{NA}\NormalTok{) \{}
\NormalTok{    self}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{name <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{name}
\NormalTok{    self}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{age <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{age}
\NormalTok{  \},}
  \DataTypeTok{print =} \ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(...) \{}
    \KeywordTok{cat}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Person: }\CharTok{\textbackslash{}n}\StringTok{"}\NormalTok{)}
    \KeywordTok{cat}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"  Name: "}\NormalTok{, self}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{name, }\StringTok{"}\CharTok{\textbackslash{}n}\StringTok{"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{sep =} \StringTok{""}\NormalTok{)}
    \KeywordTok{cat}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"  Age:  "}\NormalTok{, self}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{age, }\StringTok{"}\CharTok{\textbackslash{}n}\StringTok{"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{sep =} \StringTok{""}\NormalTok{)}
    \KeywordTok{invisible}\NormalTok{(self)}
\NormalTok{  \}}
\NormalTok{))}

\NormalTok{hadley2 <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{Person}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{new}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Hadley"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{hadley2}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
Person: 
  Name: Hadley
  Age:  NA
\end{verbatim}

Print is an S3 generic, so when print is implicitly called, it calls the method for the R6 object. The method for the R6 object is ``look for a print function inside the R6 object''

\hypertarget{classes-and-methods-14.2.3}{%
\section*{Classes and methods 14.2.3}\label{classes-and-methods-14.2.3}}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{Classes and methods 14.2.3}

\begin{question}

Once instantiated, can you add another method to an \texttt{R6} object or does the \texttt{set} function only work on the \texttt{R6} generator?

\end{question}

Once instantiated the environments are locked (no new bindings). But, you can fudge with things and still modify existing bindings if you wanted. But, this is not really something to advocate:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{Beer <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{R6}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{R6Class}\NormalTok{(}
  \StringTok{'Beer'}\NormalTok{,}
  \DataTypeTok{public =} \KeywordTok{list}\NormalTok{(}
    \DataTypeTok{abv =} \FloatTok{0.05}\NormalTok{,}
    \DataTypeTok{percent_abv =} \ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{() \{ }\KeywordTok{sprintf}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{'%.1f%%'}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{100} \OperatorTok{*}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{self}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{abv) \}}
\NormalTok{  )}
\NormalTok{)}
\KeywordTok{class}\NormalTok{(Beer)}
\CommentTok{#> [1] "R6ClassGenerator"}
\NormalTok{beer <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{Beer}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{new}\NormalTok{()}
\KeywordTok{unlockBinding}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"percent_abv"}\NormalTok{, beer)}
\NormalTok{beer}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{percent_abv <-}\StringTok{ }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{() \{ }\KeywordTok{cat}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"h@xed"}\NormalTok{)\}}
\KeywordTok{lockBinding}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"percent_abv"}\NormalTok{, beer)}
\NormalTok{beer}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{percent_abv}\NormalTok{()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] "R6ClassGenerator"
h@xed
\end{verbatim}

You can also set the lock\_objects option on the generator to FALSE

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{Beer <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{R6}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{R6Class}\NormalTok{(}
  \StringTok{'Beer'}\NormalTok{,}
  \DataTypeTok{public =} \KeywordTok{list}\NormalTok{(}
    \DataTypeTok{abv =} \FloatTok{0.05}\NormalTok{,}
    \DataTypeTok{percent_abv =} \ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{() \{ }\KeywordTok{sprintf}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{'%.1f%%'}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{100} \OperatorTok{*}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{self}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{abv) \}}
\NormalTok{  ),}
  \DataTypeTok{lock_objects =} \OtherTok{FALSE}
\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{beer <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{Beer}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{new}\NormalTok{()}
\NormalTok{beer}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{rating <-}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{5}
\NormalTok{beer}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{rating}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
## [1] 5
\end{verbatim}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] 5
\end{verbatim}

But this still won't work because the bindings were still locked

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{beer}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{percent_abv <-}\StringTok{ }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{() \{ }\KeywordTok{cat}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"h@xed"}\NormalTok{)\}}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
#> Error in beer$percent_abv <- function() {: cannot change value of locked binding for 'percent_abv'
\end{verbatim}

\hypertarget{exercises-14.2.6.4}{%
\section*{Exercises 14.2.6.4}\label{exercises-14.2.6.4}}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{Exercises 14.2.6.4}

\begin{question}

Why can't we use method chaining to access the current time zone?

\end{question}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{Timezone <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{R6Class}\NormalTok{(}
  \DataTypeTok{classname =} \StringTok{"Timezone"}\NormalTok{, }
  \DataTypeTok{public =} \KeywordTok{list}\NormalTok{(}
    \DataTypeTok{get =} \ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{() \{}
      \KeywordTok{Sys.timezone}\NormalTok{()}
\NormalTok{    \},}
    \DataTypeTok{set =} \ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(value) \{}
      \KeywordTok{stopifnot}\NormalTok{(value }\OperatorTok{%in%}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{OlsonNames}\NormalTok{())}
      
\NormalTok{      old <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{self}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{get}\NormalTok{()}
      \KeywordTok{Sys.setenv}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{TZ =}\NormalTok{ value)}
      \KeywordTok{invisible}\NormalTok{(old)}
\NormalTok{    \})}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{tz <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{Timezone}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{new}\NormalTok{()}

\NormalTok{old <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{tz}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{set}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Antarctica/South_Pole"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{tz}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{get}\NormalTok{()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] "America/Los_Angeles"
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{tz}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{set}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Antarctica/South_Pole"}\NormalTok{)}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{get}\NormalTok{()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
Error in tz$set("Antarctica/South_Pole")$get : 
  $ operator is invalid for atomic vectors
\end{verbatim}

You're not returning an R6 object in your first ``set'', you're returning a character vector, so you can't find the get method of that character vector

We can return something using the following code:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{Timezone <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{R6Class}\NormalTok{(}
  \DataTypeTok{classname =} \StringTok{"Timezone"}\NormalTok{, }
  \DataTypeTok{public =} \KeywordTok{list}\NormalTok{(}
    \DataTypeTok{get =} \ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{() \{}
\NormalTok{      self}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{current_zone}
\NormalTok{    \},}
    \DataTypeTok{set =} \ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(v) \{}
\NormalTok{      self}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{current_zone <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{v}
      \KeywordTok{invisible}\NormalTok{(self)}
\NormalTok{    \},}
    \DataTypeTok{reset =} \ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{() \{}
      \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\OperatorTok{!}\KeywordTok{is.null}\NormalTok{(private}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{.old)) \{}
\NormalTok{        self}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{current_zone <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{private}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{.old}
\NormalTok{      \}}
      \KeywordTok{invisible}\NormalTok{(self)}
\NormalTok{    \}}
\NormalTok{  ),}
  \DataTypeTok{active =} \KeywordTok{list}\NormalTok{(}
    \DataTypeTok{current_zone =} \ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(v) \{}
      \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{missing}\NormalTok{(v)) \{}
        \KeywordTok{return}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{Sys.timezone}\NormalTok{())}
\NormalTok{      \}}
      \KeywordTok{stopifnot}\NormalTok{(v }\OperatorTok{%in%}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{OlsonNames}\NormalTok{())}
\NormalTok{      old <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{Sys.timezone}\NormalTok{()}
      \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{Sys.setenv}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{TZ=}\NormalTok{v)) \{}
\NormalTok{        private}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{.old <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{old}
\NormalTok{      \} }\ControlFlowTok{else}\NormalTok{ \{}
        \KeywordTok{stop}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Unable to set timezone."}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{      \}}
      \KeywordTok{invisible}\NormalTok{(self)}
\NormalTok{    \}}
\NormalTok{  ),}
  \DataTypeTok{private =} \KeywordTok{list}\NormalTok{(}
    \DataTypeTok{.old =} \OtherTok{NULL}
\NormalTok{  )}
\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{tz <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{Timezone}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{new}\NormalTok{()}
\NormalTok{tz}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{set}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Antarctica/South_Pole"}\NormalTok{)}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{get}\NormalTok{()}
\CommentTok{#> [1] "Antarctica/South_Pole"}
\NormalTok{tz}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{reset}\NormalTok{()}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{get}\NormalTok{()}
\CommentTok{#> [1] "US/Central"}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

That said, not every function should support chaining. Sometimes you want the function to return some value (like \texttt{\$get}) and in these cases, you just won't be able to chain, and that is okay.

\hypertarget{reference-semantics}{%
\section*{14.4 Reference semantics}\label{reference-semantics}}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{14.4 Reference semantics}

\begin{question}

\begin{quote}
\$clone() does not recursively clone nested R6 objects. If you want that, you'll need to use \$clone(deep = TRUE).
\end{quote}

Can we see this in action using a subclass?

\end{question}

\hypertarget{this-example-is-taken-from-the-r6-documentation}{%
\subsubsection*{\texorpdfstring{This example is taken from the \texttt{R6} \href{https://r6.r-lib.org/articles/Introduction.html}{documentation}:}{This example is taken from the R6 documentation:}}\label{this-example-is-taken-from-the-r6-documentation}}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{This example is taken from the \texttt{R6} \href{https://r6.r-lib.org/articles/Introduction.html}{documentation}:}

Object \texttt{c1} contains \texttt{s}, which we will clone. The original and clone both point to the same object, and by using \texttt{deep\ =\ TRUE} we can modify \texttt{s} in one object without changing it in the other.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{Simple <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{R6Class}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Simple"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{public =} \KeywordTok{list}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{x =} \DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{))}

\NormalTok{Cloneable <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{R6Class}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Cloneable"}\NormalTok{,}
  \DataTypeTok{public =} \KeywordTok{list}\NormalTok{(}
    \DataTypeTok{s =} \OtherTok{NULL}\NormalTok{,}
    \DataTypeTok{initialize =} \ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{() self}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{s <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{Simple}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{new}\NormalTok{()}
\NormalTok{  )}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{c1 <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{Cloneable}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{new}\NormalTok{()}
\NormalTok{c2 <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{c1}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{clone}\NormalTok{()}

\CommentTok{# Change c1's `s` field}
\NormalTok{c1}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{s}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{x <-}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{2}

\CommentTok{# c2's `s` is the same object, so it reflects the change}
\NormalTok{c2}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{s}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{x}
\CommentTok{#> [1] 2}

\NormalTok{c3 <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{c1}\OperatorTok{$}\KeywordTok{clone}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{deep =} \OtherTok{TRUE}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{# Change c1's `s` field}
\NormalTok{c1}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{s}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{x <-}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{3}

\CommentTok{# c2's `s` is different}
\CommentTok{# if we set deep = FALSE this would be 3!}
\NormalTok{c3}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{s}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{x}
\CommentTok{#> [1] 2}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{question}

When or why would I set the clone argument to FALSE?

\end{question}

Clone has a large memory footprint so if you're going to create a lot of R6 methods you may want to exclude this!

\hypertarget{s4}{%
\chapter{S4}\label{s4}}

\hypertarget{basics}{%
\section*{15.2 Basics}\label{basics}}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{15.2 Basics}

\begin{question}

Broadly, what is a generic and method in S4 and what is their relationship?

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{setClass}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Person"}\NormalTok{, }
  \DataTypeTok{slots =} \KeywordTok{c}\NormalTok{(}
    \DataTypeTok{name =} \StringTok{"character"}\NormalTok{, }
    \DataTypeTok{age =} \StringTok{"numeric"}
\NormalTok{  )}
\NormalTok{)}

\KeywordTok{setGeneric}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age"}\NormalTok{, }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x) }\KeywordTok{standardGeneric}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age"}\NormalTok{))}
\KeywordTok{setGeneric}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age<-"}\NormalTok{, }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x, value) }\KeywordTok{standardGeneric}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age<-"}\NormalTok{))}

\KeywordTok{setMethod}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Person"}\NormalTok{, }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x) x}\OperatorTok{@}\NormalTok{age)}
\KeywordTok{setMethod}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age<-"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Person"}\NormalTok{, }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x, value) \{}
\NormalTok{  x}\OperatorTok{@}\NormalTok{age <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{value}
\NormalTok{  x}
\NormalTok{\})}

\NormalTok{john <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{new}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Person"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{name =} \StringTok{"John Smith"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{age =} \DecValTok{12}\NormalTok{)}
\KeywordTok{age}\NormalTok{(john)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] 12
\end{verbatim}

\end{question}

A generic is a function that will dispatch differently based on the class it is applied to. Above we apply the \texttt{age} generic to \texttt{Person} using \texttt{setMethod} but we could create an \texttt{age} method that behaves differently for another class, like dogs (which will add 7 to the supplied age)

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{setClass}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Person"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{slots =} \KeywordTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{name =} \StringTok{"character"}\NormalTok{,}\DataTypeTok{age =} \StringTok{"numeric"}\NormalTok{))}

\KeywordTok{setGeneric}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age"}\NormalTok{, }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x) }\KeywordTok{standardGeneric}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age"}\NormalTok{))}
\KeywordTok{setGeneric}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age<-"}\NormalTok{, }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x, value) }\KeywordTok{standardGeneric}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age<-"}\NormalTok{))}

\KeywordTok{setMethod}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Person"}\NormalTok{, }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x) x}\OperatorTok{@}\NormalTok{age)}
\KeywordTok{setMethod}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age<-"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Person"}\NormalTok{, }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x, value) \{}
\NormalTok{  x}\OperatorTok{@}\NormalTok{age <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{value}
\NormalTok{  x}
\NormalTok{\})}

\KeywordTok{setClass}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Dog"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{slots =} \KeywordTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{name =} \StringTok{"character"}\NormalTok{,  }\DataTypeTok{age =} \StringTok{"numeric"}\NormalTok{))}

\CommentTok{# You want the age generic to automatically return 7x the slot in human years}
\KeywordTok{setMethod}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Dog"}\NormalTok{, }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x) \{x}\OperatorTok{@}\NormalTok{age}\OperatorTok{*}\DecValTok{7}\NormalTok{\} ) }
\KeywordTok{setMethod}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age<-"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Dog"}\NormalTok{, }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x, value) \{}
\NormalTok{  x}\OperatorTok{@}\NormalTok{age <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{value}
\NormalTok{  x}
\NormalTok{\})}


\NormalTok{spot <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{new}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Dog"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{name =} \StringTok{"Spot Smith"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{age =} \DecValTok{12}\NormalTok{)}
\KeywordTok{age}\NormalTok{(spot)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] 84
\end{verbatim}

\begin{question}

What is \texttt{standardGeneric} doing in the example above?

\end{question}

It's the same thing as \texttt{UseMethod} but for S4

\hypertarget{exercises}{%
\section*{15.3.6.2 Exercises}\label{exercises}}
\addcontentsline{toc}{section}{15.3.6.2 Exercises}

\begin{question}

What is a virtual class and how does it relate to \texttt{setClassUnion} {[}see \texttt{?setClass}{]}

\end{question}

A virtual class is a class that cannot be instanciated. Rather than define two of the same methods for two classes, give them both a virtual parent class with the shared method.

\begin{question}

Can we make a class using \texttt{S3}, \texttt{S4}, and \texttt{R6} so we can easily directly compare the three, and their generics and methods?

\end{question}

\hypertarget{using-our-example-from-the-s4-chapter}{%

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{setClass}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Person"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{slots =} \KeywordTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{name =} \StringTok{"character"}\NormalTok{,}\DataTypeTok{age =} \StringTok{"numeric"}\NormalTok{))}

\KeywordTok{setMethod}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Person"}\NormalTok{, }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x) x}\OperatorTok{@}\NormalTok{age)}
\KeywordTok{setMethod}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age<-"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Person"}\NormalTok{, }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x, value) \{}
\NormalTok{  x}\OperatorTok{@}\NormalTok{age <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{value}
\NormalTok{  x}
\NormalTok{\})}

\KeywordTok{setClass}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Dog"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{slots =} \KeywordTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{name =} \StringTok{"character"}\NormalTok{,  }\DataTypeTok{age =} \StringTok{"numeric"}\NormalTok{))}

\CommentTok{# You want the age generic to automatically return 7x the slot in human years}
\KeywordTok{setMethod}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Dog"}\NormalTok{, }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x) \{x}\OperatorTok{@}\NormalTok{age}\OperatorTok{*}\DecValTok{7}\NormalTok{\} ) }
\KeywordTok{setMethod}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"age<-"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Dog"}\NormalTok{, }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x, value) \{}
\NormalTok{  x}\OperatorTok{@}\NormalTok{age <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{value}
\NormalTok{  x}
\NormalTok{\})}


\NormalTok{spot <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{new}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Dog"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{name =} \StringTok{"Spot Smith"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{age =} \DecValTok{12}\NormalTok{)}
\KeywordTok{age}\NormalTok{(spot)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\hypertarget{we-can-do-this-with-s3}{%

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{johnny <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{structure}\NormalTok{(}
  \KeywordTok{list}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{name =} \StringTok{"Johnny Smith"}\NormalTok{,}
       \DataTypeTok{age =} \DecValTok{12}\NormalTok{),}
  \DataTypeTok{class =} \StringTok{"s3_human"}\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{stripe <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{structure}\NormalTok{(}
  \KeywordTok{list}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{name =} \StringTok{"Stripe Smith"}\NormalTok{,}
       \DataTypeTok{age =} \DecValTok{12}\NormalTok{),}
  \DataTypeTok{class =} \StringTok{"s3_dog"}\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{s3_age <-}\StringTok{ }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x)\{}\KeywordTok{UseMethod}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"s3_age"}\NormalTok{)\}}
\NormalTok{s3_age.s3_dog <-}\StringTok{ }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x)\{x}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{age}\OperatorTok{*}\DecValTok{7}\NormalTok{\}}
\NormalTok{s3_age.s3_human <-}\StringTok{ }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x)\{x}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{age\}}

\KeywordTok{s3_age}\NormalTok{(johnny)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\NormalTok{Person <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{R6Class}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Person"}\NormalTok{, }\KeywordTok{list}\NormalTok{(}
  \DataTypeTok{name =} \OtherTok{NULL}\NormalTok{,}
  \DataTypeTok{age =} \OtherTok{NULL}\NormalTok{,}
  \DataTypeTok{initialize =} \ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(name, }\DataTypeTok{age =} \OtherTok{NA}\NormalTok{) \{}
    \KeywordTok{stopifnot}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{is.character}\NormalTok{(name), }\KeywordTok{length}\NormalTok{(name) }\OperatorTok{==}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{)}
    \KeywordTok{stopifnot}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{is.numeric}\NormalTok{(age), }\KeywordTok{length}\NormalTok{(age) }\OperatorTok{==}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{    self}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{name <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{name}
\NormalTok{    self}\OperatorTok{$}\NormalTok{age <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{age}
\NormalTok{  \}}
\NormalTok{))}

\begin{question}

I love the idea of creating templates then shoving in code using \texttt{!!} can we create a template that inserts a filtering statement into our tidypipeline?

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{# this is my template}
\NormalTok{iris }\OperatorTok{%>%}
\StringTok{  }\NormalTok{ggplot2}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{ggplot}\NormalTok{() }\OperatorTok{+}
\StringTok{  }\NormalTok{ggplot2}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{aes}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{x =}\NormalTok{ Sepal.Length, }\DataTypeTok{y =}\NormalTok{ Sepal.Width) }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }
\StringTok{  }\NormalTok{ggplot2}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{geom_point}\NormalTok{()}
\CommentTok{# somehow insert this into the template at line 2}
\NormalTok{dplyr}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{filter}\NormalTok{(Sepal.Length }\OperatorTok{>}\StringTok{ }\FloatTok{4.5}\NormalTok{) }\OperatorTok{%>%}
\CommentTok{# to create something prettier than }
\ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (x }\OperatorTok{==}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{) \{}
\NormalTok{  iris }\OperatorTok{%>%}
\StringTok{    }\NormalTok{dplyr}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{filter}\NormalTok{(Sepal.Length }\OperatorTok{>}\StringTok{ }\FloatTok{4.5}\NormalTok{) }\OperatorTok{%>%}
\StringTok{    }\NormalTok{ggplot2}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{ggplot}\NormalTok{() }\OperatorTok{+}
\StringTok{    }\NormalTok{ggplot2}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{aes}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{x =}\NormalTok{ Sepal.Length, }\DataTypeTok{y =}\NormalTok{ Sepal.Width) }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }
\StringTok{    }\NormalTok{ggplot2}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{geom_point}\NormalTok{()}
\NormalTok{\} }\ControlFlowTok{else}\NormalTok{ \{}
\NormalTok{  iris }\OperatorTok{%>%}
\StringTok{    }\NormalTok{ggplot2}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{ggplot}\NormalTok{() }\OperatorTok{+}
\StringTok{    }\NormalTok{ggplot2}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{aes}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{x =}\NormalTok{ Sepal.Length, }\DataTypeTok{y =}\NormalTok{ Sepal.Width) }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{customizable_iris <-}\StringTok{ }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{pipeline_insertion =} \OtherTok{NULL}\NormalTok{)\{}
\NormalTok{  dt <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{rlang}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{expr}\NormalTok{(iris)}
\NormalTok{  pi <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{rlang}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{enexpr}\NormalTok{(pipeline_insertion)}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\OperatorTok{!}\NormalTok{rlang}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{is_null}\NormalTok{(pi))}
\NormalTok{    dt <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{rlang}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{expr}\NormalTok{(}\OperatorTok{!!}\NormalTok{dt }\OperatorTok{%>%}\StringTok{ }\OperatorTok{!!}\NormalTok{pi)}

    \OperatorTok{!!}\NormalTok{dt }\OperatorTok{%>%}\StringTok{  }
\StringTok{      }\NormalTok{ggplot2}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{ggplot}\NormalTok{() }\OperatorTok{+}
\StringTok{      }\NormalTok{ggplot2}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{aes}\NormalTok{(}\DataTypeTok{x =}\NormalTok{ Sepal.Length, }\DataTypeTok{y =}\NormalTok{ Sepal.Width) }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }

\end{Highlighting}

\begin{verbatim}
## iris %>% dplyr::filter(Sepal.Length > 5) %>% ggplot2::ggplot() + 
##     ggplot2::aes(x = Sepal.Length, y = Sepal.Width) + ggplot2::geom_point()
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{rlang}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{eval_bare}\NormalTok{(x)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\includegraphics{17-big_picture_files/figure-latex/unnamed-chunk-3-1.pdf}

Any valid r code can be converted into an expression or list of expressions, and expressions can be patched together using this unquoting (forcing) procedure.

Probably best thoguht of in terms of the tree structure, by replacing one node with another expression:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{lobstr}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{ast}\NormalTok{(a }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{b)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
## █─`+` 
## ├─a 
## └─b
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{b <-}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{rlang}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{expr}\NormalTok{(x }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{y)}
\NormalTok{lobstr}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{ast}\NormalTok{(}\OperatorTok{!!}\NormalTok{b)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
## █─`+` 
## ├─x 
## └─y
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{lobstr}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{ast}\NormalTok{(a }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\OperatorTok{!!}\NormalTok{b)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
## █─`+` 
## ├─a 
## └─█─`+` 
##   ├─x 
##   └─y
\end{verbatim}

so the forcing operation is kind of like performing surgery on the AST, where you cut out one node (the thing being forced) and replacing it with some other code.

\hypertarget{expressions}{%
\chapter{Expressions}\label{expressions}}

\begin{question}

I understand how we can subset expression calls but why/when would you do that? What is the context for extracting stuff from a function as an expression ?

Let's build on this contrived example\ldots{}.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{x <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{read.table}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"important.csv"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{row.names =} \OtherTok{FALSE}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{lobstr}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{ast}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{read.table}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"important.csv"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{row.names =} \OtherTok{FALSE}\NormalTok{))}
\NormalTok{x[[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{]]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Making this an expression, we can use subsetting to shove in \texttt{read.csv} or \texttt{read.tsv} where \texttt{read.table} is?

\end{question}

You might need to do this in order to insert a line of code inside a function call:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{f <-}\StringTok{ }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x) \{}
  \KeywordTok{read.table}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"important.csv"}\NormalTok{, }\DataTypeTok{row.names =} \OtherTok{FALSE}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{\}}
\KeywordTok{body}\NormalTok{(f)[[}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{]][[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{]] <-}\StringTok{ }\KeywordTok{quote}\NormalTok{(read.csv)}
\NormalTok{f}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
## function (x) 
## {
##     read.csv("important.csv", row.names = FALSE)
## }
\end{verbatim}

\begin{question}

What's an application for this chapter?

\end{question}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\KeywordTok{library}\NormalTok{(rlang)}
\NormalTok{replace_sym <-}\StringTok{ }\ControlFlowTok{function}\NormalTok{(x, sym, replace) \{}
  \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is_symbol}\NormalTok{(x, }\DataTypeTok{name =}\NormalTok{ sym)) \{}
\NormalTok{    replace}
\NormalTok{  \} }\ControlFlowTok{else} \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is_atomic}\NormalTok{(x)) \{}
\NormalTok{    x}
\NormalTok{  \} }\ControlFlowTok{else} \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is_symbol}\NormalTok{(x)) \{}
\NormalTok{    x}
\NormalTok{  \} }\ControlFlowTok{else} \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is_call}\NormalTok{(x)) \{}
    \KeywordTok{as.call}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{lapply}\NormalTok{(x, replace_sym, sym, replace))}
\NormalTok{  \} }\ControlFlowTok{else} \ControlFlowTok{if}\NormalTok{ (}\KeywordTok{is.pairlist}\NormalTok{(x)) \{}
    \KeywordTok{as.pairlist}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{lapply}\NormalTok{(x, replace_sym, sym, replace))}
\NormalTok{  \} }\ControlFlowTok{else}\NormalTok{ \{}
    \KeywordTok{abort}\NormalTok{(glue}\OperatorTok{::}\KeywordTok{glue}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Don't know how to handle \{as_label(x)\}"}\NormalTok{))}
\NormalTok{  \}}
\NormalTok{\}}
\KeywordTok{replace_sym}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{expr}\NormalTok{(a }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\NormalTok{b }\OperatorTok{+}\StringTok{ }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{), }\StringTok{"b"}\NormalTok{, }\KeywordTok{expr}\NormalTok{(}\KeywordTok{f}\NormalTok{(x)))}
